2025-01-24T14:45:45.4414383Z         key=None,
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4414710Z         mode: str = "r",
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4415073Z         errors: str = "strict",

2025-01-24T14:45:45.4415908Z         start: int | None = None,
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4416310Z         stop: int | None = None,

2025-01-24T14:45:45.4417972Z         **kwargs,

2025-01-24T14:45:45.4418534Z         """
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4418890Z         Read from the store, close it if we opened it.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4419361Z     
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4419803Z         Retrieve pandas object stored in file, optionally based on where
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4420377Z         criteria.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4420730Z     
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4421207Z         .. warning::
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4421536Z     
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4422322Z            Pandas uses PyTables for reading and writing HDF5 files, which allows
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4423156Z            serializing object-dtype data with pickle when using the "fixed" format.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4423994Z            Loading pickled data received from untrusted sources can be unsafe.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4424552Z     
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4425212Z            See: https://docs.python.org/3/library/pickle.html for more.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4425772Z     
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4426040Z         Parameters
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4426346Z         ----------
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4426733Z         path_or_buf : str, path object, pandas.HDFStore
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4427418Z             Any valid string path is acceptable. Only supports the local file system,
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4428123Z             remote URLs and file-like objects are not supported.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4428590Z     
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4428998Z             If you want to pass in a path object, pandas accepts any
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4429492Z             ``os.PathLike``.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4429833Z     
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4430325Z             Alternatively, pandas accepts an open :class:`pandas.HDFStore` object.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4430896Z     
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4431371Z         key : object, optional
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4431884Z             The group identifier in the store. Can be omitted if the HDF file
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4432449Z             contains a single pandas object.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4432875Z         mode : {'r', 'r+', 'a'}, default 'r'
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4433380Z             Mode to use when opening the file. Ignored if path_or_buf is a
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4433930Z             :class:`pandas.HDFStore`. Default is 'r'.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4434373Z         errors : str, default 'strict'

2025-01-24T14:45:45.4435533Z             See the errors argument for :func:`open` for a full list
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4436033Z             of options.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4436356Z         where : list, optional
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4436739Z             A list of Term (or convertible) objects.

2025-01-24T14:45:45.4437521Z             Row number to start selection.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4437897Z         stop  : int, optional
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4438249Z             Row number to stop selection.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4438665Z         columns : list, optional
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4439054Z             A list of columns names to return.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4439485Z         iterator : bool, optional
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4439861Z             Return an iterator object.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4440256Z         chunksize : int, optional
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4440757Z             Number of rows to include in an iteration when using an iterator.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4441487Z         **kwargs
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4441879Z             Additional keyword arguments passed to HDFStore.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4442332Z     
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4442573Z         Returns
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4442837Z         -------
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4443100Z         object
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4443504Z             The selected object. Return type depends on the object stored.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4444020Z     
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4444263Z         See Also

2025-01-24T14:45:45.4445911Z     
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4446180Z         Examples
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4446479Z         --------

2025-01-24T14:45:45.4448345Z         """

2025-01-24T14:45:45.4452268Z

2025-01-24T14:45:45.4480388Z     @set_module('numpy')
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4480803Z     def load(file, mmap_mode=None, allow_pickle=False, fix_imports=True,
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4481541Z              encoding='ASCII', *, max_header_size=format._MAX_HEADER_SIZE):
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4481991Z         """
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4482413Z         Load arrays or pickled objects from ``.npy``, ``.npz`` or pickled files.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4482908Z     
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4483303Z         .. warning:: Loading files that contain object arrays uses the ``pickle``
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4484002Z                      module, which is not secure against erroneous or maliciously
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4484592Z                      constructed data. Consider passing ``allow_pickle=False`` to
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4485158Z                      load data that is known not to contain object arrays for the
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4485628Z                      safer handling of untrusted sources.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4485993Z     
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4486260Z         Parameters
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4486505Z         ----------
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4486820Z         file : file-like object, string, or pathlib.Path
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4487283Z             The file to read. File-like objects must support the
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4487752Z             ``seek()`` and ``read()`` methods and must always
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4488230Z             be opened in binary mode.  Pickled files require that the
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4488751Z             file-like object support the ``readline()`` method as well.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4489236Z         mmap_mode : {None, 'r+', 'r', 'w+', 'c'}, optional
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4489731Z             If not None, then memory-map the file, using the given mode (see
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4490285Z             `numpy.memmap` for a detailed description of the modes).  A
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4490848Z             memory-mapped array is kept on disk. However, it can be accessed
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4491604Z             and sliced like any ndarray.  Memory mapping is especially useful
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4492193Z             for accessing small fragments of large files without reading the
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4492677Z             entire file into memory.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4493031Z         allow_pickle : bool, optional
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4493548Z             Allow loading pickled object arrays stored in npy files. Reasons for
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4494205Z             disallowing pickles include security, as loading pickled data can
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4494841Z             execute arbitrary code. If pickles are disallowed, loading object
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4495363Z             arrays will fail. Default: False
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4495698Z     
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4495937Z             .. versionchanged:: 1.16.3
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4496344Z                 Made default False in response to CVE-2019-6446.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4496730Z     
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4496963Z         fix_imports : bool, optional
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4497676Z             Only useful when loading Python 2 generated pickled files on Python 3,
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4498359Z             which includes npy/npz files containing object arrays. If `fix_imports`
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4499023Z             is True, pickle will try to map the old Python 2 names to the new names
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4499674Z             used in Python 3.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4500002Z         encoding : str, optional
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4500451Z             What encoding to use when reading Python 2 strings. Only useful when
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4501244Z             loading Python 2 generated pickled files in Python 3, which includes
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4501877Z             npy/npz files containing object arrays. Values other than 'latin1',
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4502485Z             'ASCII', and 'bytes' are not allowed, as they can corrupt numerical
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4502947Z             data. Default: 'ASCII'
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4503281Z         max_header_size : int, optional
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4503765Z             Maximum allowed size of the header.  Large headers may not be safe
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4504372Z             to load securely and thus require explicitly passing a larger value.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4504895Z             See :py:func:`ast.literal_eval()` for details.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4505415Z             This option is ignored when `allow_pickle` is passed.  In that case
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4506006Z             the file is by definition trusted and the limit is unnecessary.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4506462Z     
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4506685Z         Returns
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4506926Z         -------
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4507190Z         result : array, tuple, dict, etc.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4507650Z             Data stored in the file. For ``.npz`` files, the returned instance
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4508242Z             of NpzFile class must be closed to avoid leaking file descriptors.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4508689Z     
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4508895Z         Raises
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4509126Z         ------
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4509344Z         OSError
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4509648Z             If the input file does not exist or cannot be read.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4510039Z         UnpicklingError
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4510420Z             If ``allow_pickle=True``, but the file cannot be loaded as a pickle.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4510888Z         ValueError
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4511433Z             The file contains an object array, but ``allow_pickle=False`` given.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4511920Z         EOFError
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4512287Z             When calling ``np.load`` multiple times on the same file handle,
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4512759Z             if all data has already been read
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4513087Z     
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4513302Z         See Also
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4513543Z         --------
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4513818Z         save, savez, savez_compressed, loadtxt
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4514304Z         memmap : Create a memory-map to an array stored in a file on disk.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4514909Z         lib.format.open_memmap : Create or load a memory-mapped ``.npy`` file.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4515380Z     
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4515589Z         Notes
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4515818Z         -----
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4516183Z         - If the file contains pickle data, then whatever object is stored
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4516649Z           in the pickle is returned.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4517062Z         - If the file is a ``.npy`` file, then a single array is returned.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4517603Z         - If the file is a ``.npz`` file, then a dictionary-like object is
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4518199Z           returned, containing ``{filename: array}`` key-value pairs, one for
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4518698Z           each file in the archive.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4519148Z         - If the file is a ``.npz`` file, the returned value supports the
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4519754Z           context manager protocol in a similar fashion to the open function::
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4520413Z     
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4520647Z             with load('foo.npz') as data:
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4521163Z                 a = data['a']
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4521451Z     
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4521791Z           The underlying file descriptor is closed when exiting the 'with'
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4522270Z           block.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4522503Z     
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4522902Z         Examples
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4523159Z         --------
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4523428Z         Store data to disk, and load it again:
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4523761Z     
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4524040Z         >>> np.save('/tmp/123', np.array([[1, 2, 3], [4, 5, 6]]))
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4524432Z         >>> np.load('/tmp/123.npy')
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4524755Z         array([[1, 2, 3],
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4525038Z                [4, 5, 6]])
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4525301Z     
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4525585Z         Store compressed data to disk, and load it again:
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4525970Z     
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4526202Z         >>> a=np.array([[1, 2, 3], [4, 5, 6]])
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4526555Z         >>> b=np.array([1, 2])
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4526879Z         >>> np.savez('/tmp/123.npz', a=a, b=b)
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4527234Z         >>> data = np.load('/tmp/123.npz')
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4527574Z         >>> data['a']
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4527846Z         array([[1, 2, 3],
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4528122Z                [4, 5, 6]])
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4528397Z         >>> data['b']
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4528656Z         array([1, 2])
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4528920Z         >>> data.close()
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4529186Z     
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4529516Z         Mem-map the stored array, and then access the second row
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4529944Z         directly from disk:
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4530225Z     
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4530470Z         >>> X = np.load('/tmp/123.npy', mmap_mode='r')
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4530823Z         >>> X[1, :]
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4531210Z         memmap([4, 5, 6])
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4531467Z     
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4531670Z         """
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4531942Z         if encoding not in ('ASCII', 'latin1', 'bytes'):
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4532409Z             # The 'encoding' value for pickle also affects what encoding
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4532915Z             # the serialized binary data of NumPy arrays is loaded
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4533414Z             # in. Pickle does not pass on the encoding information to
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4533920Z             # NumPy. The unpickling code in numpy._core.multiarray is
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4534472Z             # written to assume that unicode data appearing where binary
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4535009Z             # should be is in 'latin1'. 'bytes' is also safe, as is 'ASCII'.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4535437Z             #
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4535778Z             # Other encoding values can corrupt binary data, and we
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4536329Z             # purposefully disallow them. For the same reason, the errors=
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4536870Z             # argument is not exposed, as values other than 'strict'
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4537378Z             # result can similarly silently corrupt numerical data.
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4537933Z             raise ValueError("encoding must be 'ASCII', 'latin1', or 'bytes'")
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4538396Z     
2025-01-24T14:45:45.4538752Z         pickle_kwargs = dict(encoding=encoding, fix_imports=fix_imports)
